href="/wiki/Luke_Scott_(director)" title="Luke Scott (director)">Luke Scott</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Jordan_Scott" title="Jordan Scott">Jordan Scott</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Family</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Tony_Scott" title="Tony Scott">Tony Scott</a> <small>(brother; deceased)</small></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Sir Ridley Scott</b> (born 30 November 1937) is a retired English film director and producer. Following his commercial breakthrough with the science-fiction horror film <i><a href="/wiki/Alien_(film)" title="Alien (film)">Alien</a></i> (1979), further works include the <a href="/wiki/Neo-noir" title="Neo-noir">neo-noir</a> <a href="/wiki/Utopian_and_dystopian_fiction#Dystopian_fiction" title="Utopian and dystopian fiction">dystopian</a> science fiction film <i><a href="/wiki/Blade_Runner" title="Blade Runner">Blade Runner</a></i>, historical drama <i><a href="/wiki/Gladiator_(2000_film)" title="Gladiator (2000 film)">Gladiator</a></i> (which won the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Picture" title="Academy Award for Best Picture">Academy Award for Best Picture</a>), and science fiction film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Martian_(film)" title="The Martian (film)">The Martian</a></i>.\n</p><p>Scott\'s work has an atmospheric, highly concentrated visual style.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Visual_style_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Visual_style-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Though his films range widely in setting and period, they frequently showcase memorable imagery of urban environments, whether 2nd century Rome (<i>Gladiator</i>), 12th century <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Heaven_(film)" title="Kingdom of Heaven (film)">Kingdom of Heaven</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/England_in_the_Middle_Ages" title="England in the Middle Ages">Medieval England</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Robin_Hood_(2010_film)" title="Robin Hood (2010 film)">Robin Hood</a></i>), contemporary <a href="/wiki/Mogadishu" title="Mogadishu">Mogadishu</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Black_Hawk_Down_(film)" title="Black Hawk Down (film)">Black Hawk Down</a></i>), the future cityscapes of <i>Blade Runner</i>, or the distant planets in <i>Alien</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Prometheus_(2012_film)" title="Prometheus (2012 film)">Prometheus</a></i>, <i>The Martian</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Alien:_Covenant" title="Alien: Covenant">Alien: Covenant</a></i>. His films are also known for their strong female characters.<sup id="cite_ref-Heroines_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heroines-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Scott has been nominated for three <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Director" title="Academy Award for Best Director">Academy Awards for Directing</a> (for <i><a href="/wiki/Thelma_%26_Louise" title="Thelma &amp; Louise">Thelma &amp; Louise</a></i>, <i>Gladiator</i> and <i>Black Hawk Down</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> In 1995, both Ridley and his brother <a href="/wiki/Tony_Scott" title="Tony Scott">Tony</a> received a <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_Film_Awards" title="British Academy Film Awards">BAFTA</a> for Outstanding British Contribution To Cinema.<sup id="cite_ref-Outstanding_contribution_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Outstanding_contribution-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> In 2003, Scott was <a href="/wiki/Knight_Bachelor" title="Knight Bachelor">knighted</a> for his "services to the British film industry".<sup id="cite_ref-knighted_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-knighted-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> In a 2004 BBC poll Scott was named the tenth most influential person in <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Culture of the United Kingdom">British culture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In 2015 he received an honorary doctorate from the <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Art" title="Royal College of Art">Royal College of Art</a> in London. In 2018 Scott received the <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Fellowship" title="BAFTA Fellowship">BAFTA Fellowship</a> for lifetime achievement.<sup id="cite_ref-BAFTA_Felowship_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BAFTA_Felowship-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" \xe2\x80\x9d ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>\n<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"My mum brought three boys up: my dad was in the army and so he was frequently away. During the war (World War II) and post-war, we tended to travel following him around so my mum was the boss. She laid down the law and the law was God. We just said \'Yup, okay\' \xe2\x80\x93 we didn\'t argue. I think that\'s where the respect has come from, because she was tough."</div>\n<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x94  A supporter of <a href="/wiki/Girl_Power_in_popular_culture#Female_action_heroes_and_science_fiction" class="mw-redirect" title="Girl Power in popular culture">heroines</a> in his work, Scott credits his mother Elizabeth as his first female role model.<sup id="cite_ref-Female_heroes_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Female_heroes-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</p>\n</div>\n<p>Scott was born in <a href="/wiki/South_Shields" title="South Shields">South Shields</a>, County Durham, North East England,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> to Elizabeth (Williams) and Colonel Francis Percy Scott.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Born shortly before the Second World War, he was brought up in an army family. His father&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 an officer in the <a href="/wiki/Corps_of_Royal_Engineers" class="mw-redirect" title="Corps of Royal Engineers">Royal Engineers</a>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 was absent for most of his early life. His elder brother, Frank, joined the <a href="/wiki/British_Merchant_Navy" class="mw-redirect" title="British Merchant Navy">British Merchant Navy</a> when he was still young, and the pair had little contact.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> During this time the family moved around, living in (among other areas) <a href="/wiki/Cumberland" title="Cumberland">Cumberland</a> in North West England, Wales and Germany. He had a younger brother, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Scott" title="Tony Scott">Tony</a>, who also became a film director. After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the Scott family moved back to their native North East, eventually settling on Greens Beck Road in <a href="/wiki/Hartburn,_County_Durham" title="Hartburn, County Durham">Hartburn, County Durham</a>, whose industrial landscape would later inspire similar scenes in <i>Blade Runner</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> His interest in science fiction began by reading the works of <a href="/wiki/H._G._Wells" title="H. G. Wells">H. G. Wells</a> as a child.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> He studied at <a href="/wiki/Grangefield_Grammar_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Grangefield Grammar School">Grangefield Grammar School</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Hartlepool_College_of_Art" class="mw-redirect" title="West Hartlepool College of Art">West Hartlepool College of Art</a> from 1954 to 1958, obtaining a diploma in design.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="quotebox pullquote floatleft" style="width:30%;&#32;;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303512"/>\n<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"I use everything I learned every day at art school. It\'s all about white sheets of paper, pens and drawing."</div>\n<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x94  Scott speaking on the influence the <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Art" title="Royal College of Art">Royal College of Art</a> has had in designing the visuals for his films.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</p>\n</div>\n<p>Scott went on to study at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Art" title="Royal College of Art">Royal College of Art</a> in London, contributing to college magazine <i>ARK</i> and helping to establish the college film department. For his final show, he made a black and white short film, <i><a href="/wiki/Boy_and_Bicycle" title="Boy and Bicycle">Boy and Bicycle</a></i>, starring both his younger brother and his father (the film was later released on the "Extras" section of <i>The Duellists</i> DVD). In February 1963 Scott was named in title credits as "Designer" for the BBC television programme <a href="/wiki/Tonight_(1957_TV_series)" title="Tonight (1957 TV series)"><i>Tonight</i></a>, about the severe <a href="/wiki/Winter_of_1962%E2%80%9363_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Winter of 1962\xe2\x80\x9363 in the United Kingdom">winter of 1963</a>. After graduation in 1963, he secured a job as a trainee set designer with the BBC, leading to work on the popular television police series <i><a href="/wiki/Z-Cars" title="Z-Cars">Z-Cars</a></i> and science fiction series <i><a href="/wiki/Out_of_the_Unknown" title="Out of the Unknown">Out of the Unknown</a></i>. He was originally assigned to design the second <i><a href="/wiki/Doctor_Who" title="Doctor Who">Doctor Who</a></i> serial, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daleks" title="The Daleks">The Daleks</a></i>, which would have entailed realising the serial\'s eponymous alien creatures. However, shortly before Scott was due to start work, a schedule conflict meant he was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Cusick" title="Raymond Cusick">Raymond Cusick</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-scott_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scott-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> In 1965, he began directing episodes of television series for the BBC, only one of which, an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Adam_Adamant_Lives!" title="Adam Adamant Lives!">Adam Adamant Lives!</a></i>, is available commercially.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gold_Hill,_Shaftsbury,_Dorset,_England.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Gold_Hill%2C_Shaftsbury%2C_Dorset%2C_England.JPG/220px-Gold_Hill%2C_Shaftsbury%2C_Dorset%2C_England.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Gold_Hill%2C_Shaftsbury%2C_Dorset%2C_England.JPG/330px-Gold_Hill%2C_Shaftsbury%2C_Dorset%2C_England.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Gold_Hill%2C_Shaftsbury%2C_Dorset%2C_England.JPG/440px-Gold_Hill%2C_Shaftsbury%2C_Dorset%2C_England.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gold_Hill,_Shaftsbury,_Dorset,_England.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Gold_Hill,_Shaftesbury" title="Gold Hill, Shaftesbury">Gold Hill, Shaftesbury</a> in the English county of Dorset where Scott filmed the 1973 <a href="/wiki/Hovis" title="Hovis">Hovis</a> television commercial</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1968, Ridley and Tony Scott founded Ridley Scott Associates (RSA), a film and commercial production company.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Working alongside <a href="/wiki/Alan_Parker" title="Alan Parker">Alan Parker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Hudson" title="Hugh Hudson">Hugh Hudson</a> and cinematographer <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Johnson_(cinematographer)" title="Hugh Johnson (cinematographer)">Hugh Johnson</a>, Ridley Scott made many commercials at RSA during the 1970s, including a notable 1973 <a href="/wiki/Hovis" title="Hovis">Hovis</a> advertisement, "Bike Round" (underscored by the slow movement of <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._9_(Dvo%C5%99%C3%A1k)" title="Symphony No. 9 (Dvo\xc5\x99\xc3\xa1k)">Dvo\xc5\x99\xc3\xa1k\'s "New World" symphony</a> rearranged for brass), set in the north of England but filmed in <a href="/wiki/Gold_Hill,_Shaftesbury" title="Gold Hill, Shaftesbury">Gold Hill, Shaftesbury</a>, Dorset.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> A nostalgia themed television advertisement that captured the public imagination, it was voted the UK\'s all-time favourite commercial in a 2006 poll.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> In the 1970s the <a href="/wiki/Chanel_No._5" title="Chanel No. 5">Chanel No. 5</a> brand needed revitalisation having run the risk of being labelled as mass market and pass\xc3\xa9.<sup id="cite_ref-Chanel_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chanel-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Directed by Scott in the 1970s and 1980s, Chanel television commercials were inventive mini-films with production values of surreal fantasy and seduction, which "played on the same visual imagery, with the same silhouette of the bottle."<sup id="cite_ref-Chanel_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chanel-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Five members of the Scott family are directors, and all have worked for RSA.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> His brother Tony was a successful film director whose career spanned more than two decades; his sons <a href="/wiki/Jake_Scott_(director)" title="Jake Scott (director)">Jake</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luke_Scott_(director)" title="Luke Scott (director)">Luke</a> are both acclaimed directors of commercials, as is his daughter, <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Scott" title="Jordan Scott">Jordan Scott</a>. Jake and Jordan both work from Los Angeles; Luke is based in London. In 1995, <a href="/wiki/Shepperton_Studios" title="Shepperton Studios">Shepperton Studios</a> was purchased by a consortium headed by Ridley and Tony Scott, which extensively renovated the studios while also expanding and improving its grounds.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_films">Early films</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ridley_Scott&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early films">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Duellists"><i>The Duellists</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ridley_Scott&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: The Duellists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Duellists" title="The Duellists">The Duellists</a></div>\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Duellists" title="The Duellists">The Duellists</a></i> (1977) marked Ridley Scott\'s first feature film as director. Shot in Europe, it was nominated for the main prize at the <a href="/wiki/Cannes_Film_Festival" title="Cannes Film Festival">Cannes Film Festival</a>, and won an award for Best Debut Film. <i>The Duellists</i> had limited commercial impact internationally. Set during the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, it follows two French <a href="/wiki/Hussar" title="Hussar">Hussar</a> officers, D\'Hubert and Feraud (<a href="/wiki/Keith_Carradine" title="Keith Carradine">Keith Carradine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harvey_Keitel" title="Harvey Keitel">Harvey Keitel</a>) whose quarrel over an initially minor incident turns into a bitter extended feud spanning fifteen years, interwoven with the larger conflict that provides its backdrop. The film has been acclaimed for providing a historically authentic portrayal of Napoleonic uniforms and military conduct.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The 2013 release of the film on Blu-ray coincided with the publication of an essay on the film in a collection of scholarly essays on Scott.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alien"><i>Alien</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ridley_Scott&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Alien">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Alien_(film)" title="Alien (film)">Alien (film)</a></div>\n<p>Scott had originally planned next to adapt a version of <i><a href="/wiki/Tristan_and_Iseult" title="Tristan and Iseult">Tristan and Iseult</a></i>, but after seeing <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_(film)" title="Star Wars (film)">Star Wars</a></i>, he became convinced of the potential of large scale, effects-driven films. He accepted the job of directing <i><a href="/wiki/Alien_(film)" title="Alien (film)">Alien</a></i>, the 1979 horror/science-fiction film that would win him international success. Scott made the decision to switch <a href="/wiki/Ellen_Ripley" title="Ellen Ripley">Ellen Ripley</a> from the standard male action hero to a <a href="/wiki/Girl_Power_in_popular_culture#Female_action_heroes_and_science_fiction" class="mw-redirect" title="Girl Power in popular culture">heroine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Female_icon_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Female_icon-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Ripley (played by <a href="/wiki/Sigourney_Weaver" title="Sigourney Weaver">Sigourney Weaver</a>), who appeared in the first four <i>Alien</i> films, would become a cinematic icon.<sup id="cite_ref-Female_icon_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Female_icon-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The final scene of <a href="/wiki/John_Hurt" title="John Hurt">John Hurt</a>\'s character has been named by a number of publications as one of the most memorable in cinematic history.<sup id="cite_ref-memorable_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-memorable-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Filmed at <a href="/wiki/Shepperton_Studios" title="Shepperton Studios">Shepperton Studios</a> in England, <i>Alien</i> was the <a href="/wiki/1979_in_film" title="1979 in film">sixth highest-grossing film of 1979</a>, earning over $104&#160;million worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Scott was involved in the 2003 restoration and re-release of the original film. In promotional interviews at the time, Scott indicated he had been in discussions to make a fifth film in the <i>Alien</i> franchise. However, in a 2006 interview, Scott remarked that he had been unhappy about <i>Alien: The Director\'s Cut</i>, feeling that the original was "pretty flawless" and that the additions were merely a marketing tool.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Scott later returned to <i>Alien</i>-related projects when he directed <i><a href="/wiki/Prometheus_(2012_film)" title="Prometheus (2012 film)">Prometheus</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Alien:_Covenant" title="Alien: Covenant">Alien: Covenant</a></i> three decades after the original film\'s release.<sup id="cite_ref-Alien_prequel_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alien_prequel-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Blade_Runner"><i>Blade Runner</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ridley_Scott&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Blade Runner">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Blade_Runner" title="Blade Runner">Blade Runner</a></div>\n<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:27%;&#32;;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303512"/>\n<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"Outside <i>Star Wars</i>, no sci-fi universe has been etched into cinematic consciousness more thoroughly than <i><a href="/wiki/Blade_Runner" title="Blade Runner">Blade Runner</a></i>. Ridley Scott\'s definitive 1982 neo-noir offered an immersive dystopia of rain-soaked windows and shadowy buildings adorned with animated neon billboards, where flying cars hum through the endless night."</div>\n<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x94  Eric Kohn, <i>IndieWire</i>, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</p>\n</div>\n<p>After a year working on the film adaptation of <i><a href="/wiki/Dune_(novel)" title="Dune (novel)">Dune</a></i>, and following the sudden death of his brother Frank, Scott signed to direct the film version of <a href="/wiki/Philip_K._Dick" title="Philip K. Dick">Philip K. Dick</a>\'s novel <i><a href="/wiki/Do_Androids_Dream_of_Electric_Sheep%3F" title="Do Androids Dream of Electric Sheep?">Do Androids Dream of Electric Sheep?</a></i> Re-titled <i>Blade Runner</i> and starring <a href="/wiki/Harrison_Ford" title="Harrison Ford">Harrison Ford</a>, the film was a commercial disappointment in cinemas in 1982, but is now regarded as a classic.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> In 1991, Scott\'s notes were used by Warner Brothers to create a rushed <a href="/wiki/Director%27s_cut" title="Director&#39;s cut">director\'s cut</a> which removed the main character\'s voiceover and made a number of other small changes, including to the ending. Later Scott personally supervised a digital restoration of <i>Blade Runner</i> and approved what was called <i>The Final Cut</i>. This version was released in Los Angeles, New York City and <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a> cinemas on 5 October 2007, and as an elaborate DVD release in December 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-bladerunner2007_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bladerunner2007-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Today, <i>Blade Runner</i> is ranked by many critics as one of the most important and influential science fiction films ever made,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> partly thanks to its much imitated portraits of a future cityscape.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> It is often discussed along with <a href="/wiki/William_Gibson" title="William Gibson">William Gibson</a>\'s novel <i><a href="/wiki/Neuromancer" title="Neuromancer">Neuromancer</a></i> as initiating the <a href="/wiki/Cyberpunk" title="Cyberpunk">cyberpunk</a> genre. Scott has described <i>Blade Runner</i> as his "most complete and personal film".<sup id="cite_ref-scottobserver_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scottobserver-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id=".221984.22_Apple_Macintosh_commercial"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;1984&quot;_Apple_Macintosh_commercial">"1984" Apple Macintosh commercial</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ridley_Scott&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: &quot;1984&quot; Apple Macintosh commercial">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1984_(advertisement)" title="1984 (advertisement)">1984 (advertisement)</a></div>\n<p>In 1984, Scott directed a big-budget ($900,000) television commercial, "<a href="/wiki/1984_(advertisement)" title="1984 (advertisement)">1984</a>", to launch <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Apple_Macintosh" class="mw-redirect" title="Apple Macintosh">Macintosh</a> computer.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Scott filmed the advertisement in England for about $370,000;<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> which was given a showcase airing in the US on 22 January 1984, during <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XVIII" title="Super Bowl XVIII">Super Bowl XVIII</a>, alongside screenings in cinemas.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Some consider this advertisement a "watershed event" in advertising<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> and a "masterpiece".<sup id="cite_ref-masterpiece_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-masterpiece-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Advertising_Age" title="Advertising Age">Advertising Age</a></i> placed it top of its list of the 50 greatest commercials.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Set in a dystopian future modelled after <a href="/wiki/George_Orwell" title="George Orwell">George Orwell</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Nineteen_Eighty-Four" title="Nineteen Eighty-Four">Nineteen Eighty-Four</a></i>, Scott\'s advertisement used its heroine (portrayed by English athlete <a href="/wiki/Anya_Major" title="Anya Major">Anya Major</a>) to represent the coming of the Macintosh (indicated by her white <a href="/wiki/Sleeveless_shirt" title="Sleeveless shirt">tank top</a> adorned with a picture of the Apple Macintosh computer) as a means of saving humanity from "conformity" (<a href="/wiki/Big_Brother_(1984)" class="mw-redirect" title="Big Brother (1984)">Big Brother</a>), an allusion to <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>, at that time the dominant force in computing.<sup id="cite_ref-cellini_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cellini-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legend"><i>Legend</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ridley_Scott&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Legend">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Legend_(1985_film)" title="Legend (1985 film)">Legend (1985 film)</a></div>\n<p>In 1985, Scott directed <i><a href="/wiki/Legend_(1985_film)" title="Legend (1985 film)">Legend</a></i>, a fantasy film produced by <a href="/wiki/Arnon_Milchan" title="Arnon Milchan">Arnon Milchan</a>. Scott decided to create a "once upon a time" tale set in a world of princesses, unicorns and goblins, filming almost entirely inside the studio. Scott cast <a href="/wiki/Tom_Cruise" title="Tom Cruise">Tom Cruise</a> as the film\'s hero, Jack, <a href="/wiki/Mia_Sara" title="Mia Sara">Mia Sara</a> as Princess Lili and <a href="/wiki/Tim_Curry" title="Tim Curry">Tim Curry</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Satan" title="Satan">Satan</a>-horned Lord of Darkness.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Scott had a forest set built on the <a href="/wiki/007_Stage" title="007 Stage">007 Stage</a> at <a href="/wiki/Pinewood_Studios" title="Pinewood Studios">Pinewood Studios</a> in Buckinghamshire, with trees 60 feet high and trunks 30 feet in diameter.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> In the final stages of filming, the forest set was destroyed by fire; <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Goldsmith" title="Jerry Goldsmith">Jerry Goldsmith</a>\'s original score was used for European release, but replaced in North America with a score by <a href="/wiki/Tangerine_Dream" title="Tangerine Dream">Tangerine Dream</a>. Rob Bottin provided the film\'s Academy Award-nominated make-up effects, most notably Curry\'s red-coloured Satan figure. Though a major commercial failure on release, the film has gone on to become a <a href="/wiki/Cult_classic" class="mw-redirect" title="Cult classic">cult classic</a>. The 2002 Director\'s Cut restored Goldsmith\'s original score.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Subsequent_films">Subsequent films</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ridley_Scott&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Subsequent films">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span id="1987.E2.80.931992"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1987\xe2\x80\x931992">1987\xe2\x80\x931992</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ridley_Scott&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 1987\xe2\x80\x931992">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Scott made <i><a href="/wiki/Someone_to_Watch_Over_Me_(film)" title="Someone to Watch Over Me (film)">Someone to Watch Over Me</a></i>, a romantic thriller starring <a href="/wiki/Tom_Berenger" title="Tom Berenger">Tom Berenger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mimi_Rogers" title="Mimi Rogers">Mimi Rogers</a> in 1987, and <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Rain_(1989_American_film)" title="Black Rain (1989 American film)">Black Rain</a></i> (1989), a police drama starring <a href="/wiki/Michael_Douglas" title="Michael Douglas">Michael Douglas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andy_Garc%C3%ADa" title="Andy Garc\xc3\xada">Andy Garc\xc3\xada</a>, shot partially in Japan. Both achieved mild success at the box office. <i>Black Rain</i> was the first of Scott\'s six collaborations with the composer <a href="/wiki/Hans_Zimmer" title="Hans Zimmer">Hans Zimmer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The road film <i><a href="/wiki/Thelma_%26_Louise" title="Thelma &amp; Louise">Thelma &amp; Louise</a></i> (1991) starring <a href="/wiki/Geena_Davis" title="Geena Davis">Geena Davis</a> as Thelma, <a href="/wiki/Susan_Sarandon" title="Susan Sarandon">Susan Sarandon</a> as Louise, in addition to the breakthrough role for <a href="/wiki/Brad_Pitt" title="Brad Pitt">Brad Pitt</a>\nas J.D, proved to be one of Scott\'s biggest critical successes, helping revive the director\'s reputation and receiving his first nomination for the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Director" title="Academy Award for Best Director">Academy Award for Best Director</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> His next project, independently-funded historical epic <i><a href="/wiki/1492:_Conquest_of_Paradise" title="1492: Conquest of Paradise">1492: Conquest of Paradise</a></i>, was a box office failure. The film recounts the expeditions to the Americas by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> (French star <a href="/wiki/G%C3%A9rard_Depardieu" title="G\xc3\xa9rard Depardieu">G\xc3\xa9rard Depardieu</a>). Scott did not release another film for four years.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1993.E2.80.931999"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1993\xe2\x80\x931999">1993\xe2\x80\x931999</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ridley_Scott&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 1993\xe2\x80\x931999">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1995, Ridley and his brother Tony formed a production company, <a href="/wiki/Scott_Free_Productions" title="Scott Free Productions">Scott Free Productions</a>, in Los Angeles. All Ridley\'s subsequent feature films, starting with <i><a href="/wiki/White_Squall_(film)" title="White Squall (film)">White Squall</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/G.I._Jane" title="G.I. Jane">G.I. Jane</a></i>, have been produced under the <a href="/wiki/Scott_Free_Productions" title="Scott Free Productions">Scott Free</a> banner. In 1995 the two brothers purchased a controlling interest in the British film studio <a href="/wiki/Shepperton_Studios" title="Shepperton Studios">Shepperton Studios</a>. In 2001, Shepperton merged with <a href="/wiki/Pinewood_Studios" title="Pinewood Studios">Pinewood Studios</a> to become <a href="/wiki/The_Pinewood_Studios_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="The Pinewood Studios Group">The Pinewood Studios Group</a>, which is headquartered in Buckinghamshire, England.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2000.E2.80.932005"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2000\xe2\x80\x932005">2000\xe2\x80\x932005</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ridley_Scott&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2000\xe2\x80\x932005">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Scott\'s historical drama <i><a href="/wiki/Gladiator_(2000_film)" title="Gladiator (2000 film)">Gladiator</a></i> (2000) proved to be one of his biggest critical and commercial successes. It won five Academy Awards, including Best Picture, Best Actor for the film\'s star <a href="/wiki/Russell_Crowe" title="Russell Crowe">Russell Crowe</a>, and saw Scott nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Director" title="Academy Award for Best Director">Academy Award for Best Director</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Scott worked with British visual effects company <a href="/wiki/The_Mill_(post-production)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Mill (post-production)">The Mill</a> for the film\'s computer-generated imagery, and the film was dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Reed" title="Oliver Reed">Oliver Reed</a> who died during filming \xe2\x80\x93 The Mill created a digital body double for Reed\'s remaining scenes.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Some have credited <i>Gladiator </i> with reviving the nearly defunct "<a href="/wiki/Sword_and_sandal" class="mw-redirect" title="Sword and sandal">sword and sandal</a>" historical genre. The film was named the fifth best action film of all time in the <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a> special <i><a href="/wiki/Best_in_Film:_The_Greatest_Movies_of_Our_Time" title="Best in Film: The Greatest Movies of Our Time">Best in Film: The Greatest Movies of Our Time</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Scott directed <i><a href="/wiki/Hannibal_(film)" title="Hannibal (film)">Hannibal</a></i> (2001) starring <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Hopkins" title="Anthony Hopkins">Anthony Hopkins</a> as Hannibal Lecter. The film was commercially successful despite receiving mixed reviews. Scott\'s next film, <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Hawk_Down_(film)" title="Black Hawk Down (film)">Black Hawk Down</a></i> (2001), featuring <a href="/wiki/Tom_Hardy" title="Tom Hardy">Tom Hardy</a> in his film debut, was based on a group of stranded US soldiers fighting for their lives in <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>; Scott was nominated for an Oscar for Best Director.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> In 2003, Scott directed a smaller scale project, <i><a href="/wiki/Matchstick_Men" title="Matchstick Men">Matchstick Men</a></i>, adapted from the novel by <a href="/wiki/Eric_Garcia" title="Eric Garcia">Eric Garcia</a> and starring <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Cage" title="Nicolas Cage">Nicolas Cage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sam_Rockwell" title="Sam Rockwell">Sam Rockwell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alison_Lohman" title="Alison Lohman">Alison Lohman</a>. It received mostly positive reviews, but performed moderately at the box office.\n</p><p>In 2005, he made the modestly successful <i><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Heaven_(film)" title="Kingdom of Heaven (film)">Kingdom of Heaven</a></i>, a film about the <a href="/wiki/Crusades" title="Crusades">Crusades</a>. The film starred <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Bloom" title="Orlando Bloom">Orlando Bloom</a>, and marked Scott\'s first collaboration with the composer <a href="/wiki/Harry_Gregson-Williams" title="Harry Gregson-Williams">Harry Gregson-Williams</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HG_Williams_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HG_Williams-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The Moroccan government sent the Moroccan cavalry as extras for some battle scenes.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Unhappy with the theatrical version of <i>Kingdom of Heaven</i> (which he blamed on paying too much attention to the opinions of preview audiences in addition to relenting when Fox wanted 45 minutes shaved off), Scott supervised a director\'s cut of the film, the true version of what he wanted, which was released on DVD in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The director\'s cut of <i>Kingdom of Heaven</i> has been met with critical acclaim, with <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" title="Empire (film magazine)">Empire</a></i> magazine calling the film an "epic", adding: "The added 45 minutes in the director\xe2\x80\x99s cut are like pieces missing from a beautiful but incomplete puzzle."<sup id="cite_ref-Kingdom_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kingdom-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> "This is the one that should have gone out" reflected Scott.<sup id="cite_ref-Kingdom_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kingdom-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Asked if he was against previewing in general in 2006, Scott stated: "It depends who\'s in the driving seat. If you\'ve got a lunatic doing my job, then you need to preview. But a good director should be experienced enough to judge what he thinks is the correct version to go out into the cinema."<sup id="cite_ref-totalfilm_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-totalfilm-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_and_upcoming_films">Recent and upcoming films</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ridley_Scott&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Recent and upcoming films">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span id="2006.E2.80.932011"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2006\xe2\x80\x932011">2006\xe2\x80\x932011</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ridley_Scott&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 2006\xe2\x80\x932011">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Scott teamed up again with <i>Gladiator</i> star <a href="/wiki/Russell_Crowe" title="Russell Crowe">Russell Crowe</a>, for <i><a href="/wiki/A_Good_Year" title="A Good Year">A Good Year</a></i>, based on the best-selling book by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Mayle" title="Peter Mayle">Peter Mayle</a> about an investment banker who finds a new life in <a href="/wiki/Provence" title="Provence">Provence</a>. The film was released on 10 November 2006. A few days later <a href="/wiki/Rupert_Murdoch" title="Rupert Murdoch">Rupert Murdoch</a>, chairman of studio <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox" title="20th Century Fox">20th Century Fox</a> (who backed the film) dismissed <i>A Good Year</i> as "a flop" at a shareholders\' meeting.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Scott\'s next film was <i><a href="/wiki/American_Gangster_(film)" title="American Gangster (film)">American Gangster</a></i>, based on the story of real-life drug kingpin <a href="/wiki/Frank_Lucas_(drug_dealer)" title="Frank Lucas (drug dealer)">Frank Lucas</a>. Scott took over the project in early 2006, and had screenwriter <a href="/wiki/Steven_Zaillian" title="Steven Zaillian">Steven Zaillian</a> rewrite his script to focus on the dynamic between Frank Lucas and <a href="/wiki/Richie_Roberts" title="Richie Roberts">Richie Roberts</a>. <a href="/wiki/Denzel_Washington" title="Denzel Washington">Denzel Washington</a> signed on to the project as Lucas, with Russell Crowe co-starring. The film premiered in November 2007 to positive reviews and box office success, and Scott was nominated for a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Director" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Director">Golden Globe for Best Director</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In late 2008, Scott\'s espionage thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Body_of_Lies_(film)" title="Body of Lies (film)">Body of Lies</a></i>, starring <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_DiCaprio" title="Leonardo DiCaprio">Leonardo DiCaprio</a> and Russell Crowe, opened to lukewarm ticket-sales and mixed reviews. Scott directed a revisionist adaptation of <i><a href="/wiki/Robin_Hood_(2010_film)" title="Robin Hood (2010 film)">Robin Hood</a></i>, which starred Russell Crowe as <a href="/wiki/Robin_Hood" title="Robin Hood">Robin Hood</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cate_Blanchett" title="Cate Blanchett">Cate Blanchett</a> as <a href="/wiki/Maid_Marian" title="Maid Marian">Maid Marian</a>. It was released in May 2010 to mixed reviews, but a respectable box-office.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ridley_Scott,_Charlize_Theron_%26_Michael_Fassbender_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Ridley_Scott%2C_Charlize_Theron_%26_Michael_Fassbender_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg/220px-Ridley_Scott%2C_Charlize_Theron_%26_Michael_Fassbender_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Ridley_Scott%2C_Charlize_Theron_%26_Michael_Fassbender_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg/330px-Ridley_Scott%2C_Charlize_Theron_%26_Michael_Fassbender_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Ridley_Scott%2C_Charlize_Theron_%26_Michael_Fassbender_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg/440px-Ridley_Scott%2C_Charlize_Theron_%26_Michael_Fassbender_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ridley_Scott,_Charlize_Theron_%26_Michael_Fassbender_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Scott speaking with <i><a href="/wiki/Prometheus_(2012_film)" title="Prometheus (2012 film)">Prometheus</a></i> stars <a href="/wiki/Charlize_Theron" title="Charlize Theron">Charlize Theron</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Fassbender" title="Michael Fassbender">Michael Fassbender</a> at Wondercon 2012 in Anaheim, California on 17 March 2012</div></div></div>\n<p>On 31 July 2009, news surfaced of a two-part prequel to <i>Alien</i> with Scott attached to direct.<sup id="cite_ref-Alien_prequel_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alien_prequel-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The project, ultimately reduced to a single film called <i><a href="/wiki/Prometheus_(2012_film)" title="Prometheus (2012 film)">Prometheus</a></i>, which Scott described as sharing "strands of <i>Alien\'</i>s DNA" while not being a direct prequel, was released in June 2012. The film starred <a href="/wiki/Charlize_Theron" title="Charlize Theron">Charlize Theron</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Fassbender" title="Michael Fassbender">Michael Fassbender</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Noomi_Rapace" title="Noomi Rapace">Noomi Rapace</a> playing the leading role of the scientist named Elizabeth Shaw. The film received mostly positive reviews and grossed $403&#160;million at the box office.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 2009, Scott planned to direct an adaptation of <a href="/wiki/Aldous_Huxley" title="Aldous Huxley">Aldous Huxley</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Brave_New_World" title="Brave New World">Brave New World</a></i> set in a <a href="/wiki/Dystopian" class="mw-redirect" title="Dystopian">dystopian</a> London with <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_DiCaprio" title="Leonardo DiCaprio">Leonardo DiCaprio</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, the TV Series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Good_Wife" title="The Good Wife">The Good Wife</a></i> premiered with Ridley and his brother <a href="/wiki/Tony_Scott" title="Tony Scott">Tony</a> credited as executive producers. On 6 July 2010, YouTube announced the launch of <i><a href="/wiki/Life_in_a_Day_(YouTube)" class="mw-redirect" title="Life in a Day (YouTube)">Life in a Day</a></i>, an experimental documentary executive produced by Scott. Released at the <a href="/wiki/Sundance_Film_Festival" title="Sundance Film Festival">Sundance Film Festival</a> on 27 January 2011, it incorporates footage shot on 24 July 2010 submitted by YouTube users from around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> As part of the buildup to the <a href="/wiki/2012_London_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="2012 London Olympics">2012 London Olympics</a>, Scott produced <i><a href="/wiki/Britain_in_a_Day" title="Britain in a Day">Britain in a Day</a></i>, a documentary film consisting of footage shot by the British public on 12 November 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2012.E2.80.93present"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2012\xe2\x80\x93present">2012\xe2\x80\x93present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ridley_Scott&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 2012\xe2\x80\x93present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2012, Scott produced the commercial for <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a>\'s fragrance, "<a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga_Fame" title="Lady Gaga Fame">Fame</a>." It was touted as the first ever black Eau de Parfum, in the informal credits attached to the trailer for this advertisement. On 24 June 2013, Scott\'s series <i>Crimes of the Century</i> debuted on <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> In November 2012 it was announced that Scott would produce the documentary, <i><a href="/wiki/Springsteen_%26_I" title="Springsteen &amp; I">Springsteen &amp; I</a></i> directed by <a href="/wiki/Baillie_Walsh" title="Baillie Walsh">Baillie Walsh</a> and inspired by <i>Life in a Day</i>, which Scott also produced. The film featured fan footage from throughout the world on what musician <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen" title="Bruce Springsteen">Bruce Springsteen</a> meant to them and how he impacted their lives.<sup id="cite_ref-Springsteen_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Springsteen-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The film was released for one day only in 50 countries and on over 2000 film screens on 22 July 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Springsteen_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Springsteen-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Scott directed <i><a href="/wiki/The_Counselor" title="The Counselor">The Counselor</a></i> (2013), with a screenplay by author <a href="/wiki/Cormac_McCarthy" title="Cormac McCarthy">Cormac McCarthy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FirstImage_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FirstImage-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> On 25 October 2013, <i>Indiewire</i> reported that "Before McCarthy sold his first spec script for Scott\'s (<i>Counselor</i>) film, the director was heavily involved in developing an adaptation of the author\'s 1985 novel <i><a href="/wiki/Blood_Meridian" title="Blood Meridian">Blood Meridian</a></i> with screenwriter <a href="/wiki/William_Monahan" title="William Monahan">Bill Monahan</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Departed" title="The Departed">The Departed</a></i>). But as Scott said in a <i>Time Out</i> interview, \'[Studios] didn\'t want to make it. The book is so uncompromising, which is what\'s great about it.\' Described as an \'anti-western\'..."<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Scott directed the <a href="/wiki/List_of_films_based_on_the_Bible" title="List of films based on the Bible">biblically-inspired</a> <a href="/wiki/Epic_film" title="Epic film">epic film</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Exodus:_Gods_and_Kings" title="Exodus: Gods and Kings">Exodus: Gods and Kings</a></i>, released in December 2014 which received mixed-to-negative reviews from critics while earning $268 million on a $140 million budget. Filmed at <a href="/wiki/Pinewood_Studios" title="Pinewood Studios">Pinewood Studios</a> in Buckinghamshire, the film starred <a href="/wiki/Christian_Bale" title="Christian Bale">Christian Bale</a> in the lead role.<sup id="cite_ref-Houses_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Houses-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NASA_Journey_to_Mars_and_%E2%80%9CThe_Martian%22_(201508180003HQ).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/NASA_Journey_to_Mars_and_%E2%80%9CThe_Martian%22_%28201508180003HQ%29.jpg/220px-NASA_Journey_to_Mars_and_%E2%80%9CThe_Martian%22_%28201508180003HQ%29.jpg" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/NASA_Journey_to_Mars_and_%E2%80%9CThe_Martian%22_%28201508180003HQ%29.jpg/330px-NASA_Journey_to_Mars_and_%E2%80%9CThe_Martian%22_%28201508180003HQ%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/NASA_Journey_to_Mars_and_%E2%80%9CThe_Martian%22_%28201508180003HQ%29.jpg/440px-NASA_Journey_to_Mars_and_%E2%80%9CThe_Martian%22_%28201508180003HQ%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2666" data-file-height="2666" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NASA_Journey_to_Mars_and_%E2%80%9CThe_Martian%22_(201508180003HQ).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Scott participates in a question and answer session about NASA\xe2\x80\x99s journey to Mars and his film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Martian_(film)" title="The Martian (film)">The Martian</a></i>, 18 August 2015</div></div></div>\n<p>In May 2014, Scott began negotiations to direct <i><a href="/wiki/The_Martian_(film)" title="The Martian (film)">The Martian</a></i>, starring <a href="/wiki/Matt_Damon" title="Matt Damon">Matt Damon</a> as Mark Watney.<sup id="cite_ref-holl_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-holl-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Like many of Scott\'s previous works, <i>The Martian</i> features a heroine in the form of <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Chastain" title="Jessica Chastain">Jessica Chastain</a>\'s character who is the mission commander.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The film was originally scheduled for release on 25 November 2015, but Fox later switched its release date with that of <a href="/wiki/Victor_Frankenstein_(film)" title="Victor Frankenstein (film)"><i>Victor Frankenstein</i></a>, and thus <i>The Martian</i> was released on 2 October 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-firstshow_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-firstshow-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>  <i>The Martian</i> was a critical and commercial success, grossed over $630&#160;million worldwide, becoming Scott\'s highest-grossing film to date.<sup id="cite_ref-Box_office_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Box_office-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A sequel to <i>Prometheus</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Alien:_Covenant" title="Alien: Covenant">Alien: Covenant</a></i>, started filming in 2016, premiered in London on 4 May 2017, and received general release on 19 May 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> The film received generally positive reviews from critics, with many praising <a href="/wiki/Michael_Fassbender" title="Michael Fassbender">Michael Fassbender</a>\'s dual performance and calling the film a return to form for both director Ridley Scott and the franchise.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 2011, information leaked about production of a <a href="/wiki/Blade_Runner_2049" title="Blade Runner 2049">sequel</a> to <i>Blade Runner</i> by <a href="/wiki/Alcon_Entertainment" title="Alcon Entertainment">Alcon Entertainment</a>, with Alcon partners <a href="/wiki/Broderick_Johnson" title="Broderick Johnson">Broderick Johnson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Kosove" title="Andrew Kosove">Andrew Kosove</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Scott informed the <i>Variety</i> publication in November 2014 that he was no longer the director for the film and would only fulfill a producer\'s role. Scott also revealed that filming would begin sometime within 2015, and that <a href="/wiki/Harrison_Ford" title="Harrison Ford">Harrison Ford</a> has signed on to reprise his role from the original film but his character should only appear in "the third act" of the sequel.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> On 26 February 2015, the sequel was officially confirmed, with <a href="/wiki/Denis_Villeneuve" title="Denis Villeneuve">Denis Villeneuve</a> hired to direct the film, and Scott being an executive producer.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The sequel, <i><a href="/wiki/Blade_Runner_2049" title="Blade Runner 2049">Blade Runner 2049</a></i>, was released on 6 October 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-oculus_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oculus-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From May to August 2017, Scott filmed <i><a href="/wiki/All_the_Money_in_the_World" title="All the Money in the World">All the Money in the World</a>,</i> a drama about the kidnapping of <a href="/wiki/John_Paul_Getty_III" title="John Paul Getty III">John Paul Getty III</a>, starring <a href="/wiki/Mark_Wahlberg" title="Mark Wahlberg">Mark Wahlberg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Williams_(actress)" title="Michelle Williams (actress)">Michelle Williams</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Spacey" title="Kevin Spacey">Kevin Spacey</a> originally portrayed Getty Sr. However, after multiple sexual assault allegations against the actor, Scott made the decision to replace him with <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Plummer" title="Christopher Plummer">Christopher Plummer</a>, saying "You can\'t condone that kind of behaviour in any shape or form. We cannot let one person\'s action affect the good work of all these other people. It\'s that simple."<sup id="cite_ref-Spacey_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spacey-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Scott began re-shooting Spacey\'s scenes with Plummer on 20 November, which included filming at <a href="/wiki/Elveden_Hall" title="Elveden Hall">Elveden Hall</a> in west Suffolk, England.<sup id="cite_ref-Spacey_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spacey-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> With a release date of 25 December 2017, the film studio had its doubts that Scott would manage it, saying: "They were like, \'You\'ll never do it. God be with you.\'"<sup id="cite_ref-Spacey_94-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spacey-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_projects">Future projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ridley_Scott&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Future projects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In January 2016, Scott was in early negotiations to direct the screen version of the 1968 British TV series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Prisoner" title="The Prisoner">The Prisoner</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> In May 2016, it was announced that Scott and <a href="/wiki/Drew_Goddard" title="Drew Goddard">Drew Goddard</a> (who had worked together on <i>The Martian</i>) would be reteaming to adapt the book <i><a href="/wiki/S._Craig_Zahler#Novels" title="S. Craig Zahler">Wraiths of the Broken Land</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/S._Craig_Zahler" title="S. Craig Zahler">S. Craig Zahler</a>. It is described as a piece of fiction that combines elements of "horror, noir, and Asian ultra-violence."<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> In April 2017, 20th Century Fox lined up Scott to direct a film about the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Britain" title="Battle of Britain">Battle of Britain</a> from WWII, where the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> defended the country from German <a href="/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">Luftwaffe</a> attacks, which is described as a "passion project" for the director.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Scott has said that a sequel to <i>Alien: Covenant</i> would film 14 months from May 2017. It will be the final film in his <a href="/wiki/Alien_(franchise)#Prequel_series" title="Alien (franchise)">prequel series</a> to his original film, <i>Alien</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> As of September 2018 there has been no update on the film development. On 4 January 2018, it was reported that Scott is in talks to direct a <a href="/wiki/Disney" class="mw-redirect" title="Disney">Disney</a> film adaptation of <i><a href="/wiki/T._A._Barron#The_Merlin_Saga" title="T. A. Barron">The Merlin Saga</a></i>, which is based on a 12-book series written by <a href="/wiki/T._A._Barron" title="T. A. Barron">T. A. Barron</a>, with a screenplay from <a href="/wiki/Philippa_Boyens" title="Philippa Boyens">Philippa Boyens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> On 15 March it was reported that Scott is in talks to adapt Greg Rucka\'s graphic novel <i><a href="/wiki/Queen_%26_Country" title="Queen &amp; Country">Queen &amp; Country</a></i> for 20th Century Fox.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Television_projects">Television projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ridley_Scott&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Television projects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Ridley Scott and his brother Tony produced <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> series <i><a href="/wiki/Numb3rs" class="mw-redirect" title="Numb3rs">Numb3rs</a></i> (2005\xe2\x80\x9310), a crime drama about a genius mathematician who helps the <a href="/wiki/FBI" class="mw-redirect" title="FBI">FBI</a> solve crimes; and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Good_Wife" title="The Good Wife">The Good Wife</a></i> (2009\xe2\x80\x932016), a legal drama about an attorney balancing her job with her husband, a former state attorney trying to rebuild his political career after a major scandal. The two Scotts also produced a 2010 <a href="/wiki/The_A-Team_(film)" title="The A-Team (film)">film adaptation</a> of 1980s television show <i><a href="/wiki/The_A-Team" title="The A-Team">The A-Team</a></i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Joe_Carnahan" title="Joe Carnahan">Joe Carnahan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Ridley Scott was an executive producer of the first season of Amazon\'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Man_in_the_High_Castle_(TV_series)" title="The Man in the High Castle (TV series)">The Man in the High Castle</a></i> (2015\xe2\x80\x9316).<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Through <a href="/wiki/Scott_Free_Productions" title="Scott Free Productions">Scott Free Productions</a>, he is an executive producer on the dark comic science-fiction series <i><a href="/wiki/BrainDead_(TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="BrainDead (TV series)">BrainDead</a></i> which debuted on CBS in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 20 November 2017, Amazon struck a deal with AMC Studios for a worldwide release of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Terror_(TV_series)" title="The Terror (TV series)">The Terror</a></i>, Scott\'s series adaptation of <a href="/wiki/The_Terror_(novel)" title="The Terror (novel)">Dan Simmons\' novel</a>, a speculative retelling of British explorer Sir <a href="/wiki/John_Franklin" title="John Franklin">John Franklin</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Franklin%27s_lost_expedition" title="Franklin&#39;s lost expedition">lost expedition</a> of <a href="/wiki/HMS_Erebus_(1826)" title="HMS Erebus (1826)">HMS <i>Erebus</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/HMS_Terror_(1813)" title="HMS Terror (1813)">HMS <i>Terror</i></a> to the <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a> in 1845\xe2\x80\x931848 to force the <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Passage" title="Northwest Passage">Northwest Passage</a>, with elements of horror and supernatural fiction), with the series set for release in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ridley_Scott&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%27The_Martian%27_World_Premiere_(NHQ201509110014).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/%27The_Martian%27_World_Premiere_%28NHQ201509110014%29.jpg/220px-%27The_Martian%27_World_Premiere_%28NHQ201509110014%29.jpg" width="220" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/%27The_Martian%27_World_Premiere_%28NHQ201509110014%29.jpg/330px-%27The_Martian%27_World_Premiere_%28NHQ201509110014%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/%27The_Martian%27_World_Premiere_%28NHQ201509110014%29.jpg/440px-%27The_Martian%27_World_Premiere_%28NHQ201509110014%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3120" data-file-height="2400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%27The_Martian%27_World_Premiere_(NHQ201509110014).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Scott with his partner Giannina Facio at the world premiere of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Martian_(film)" title="The Martian (film)">The Martian</a></i> held at the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_International_Film_Festival" title="Toronto International Film Festival">Toronto International Film Festival</a> on 11 September 2015</div></div></div>\n<p>Ridley Scott was married to Felicity Heywood from 1964 to 1975. The couple had two sons, <a href="/wiki/Jake_Scott_(director)" title="Jake Scott (director)">Jake</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luke_Scott_(director)" title="Luke Scott (director)">Luke</a>, both of whom work as directors on Scott\'s production company, Ridley Scott Associates. Scott later married advertising executive Sandy Watson in 1979, with whom he had a daughter, <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Scott" title="Jordan Scott">Jordan Scott</a>, and divorced in 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> His current partner is actress <a href="/wiki/Giannina_Facio" title="Giannina Facio">Giannina Facio</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> whom he has cast in all his films since <i><a href="/wiki/White_Squall_(film)" title="White Squall (film)">White Squall</a></i> except <i><a href="/wiki/American_Gangster_(film)" title="American Gangster (film)">American Gangster</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Martian_(film)" title="The Martian (film)">The Martian</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> He divides his time between homes in London, France, and Los Angeles.<sup id="cite_ref-Houses_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Houses-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>His eldest brother Frank died, aged 45, of skin cancer in 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> His younger brother <a href="/wiki/Tony_Scott" title="Tony Scott">Tony</a>, who was also his business partner in their company <a href="/wiki/Scott_Free_Productions" title="Scott Free Productions">Scott Free</a>, died on 19 August 2012 at the age of 68 after jumping from the <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Thomas_Bridge" title="Vincent Thomas Bridge">Vincent Thomas Bridge</a> which spans Los Angeles Harbor, after an originally disputed long struggle with cancer.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Before Tony\'s death, he and Ridley collaborated on a <a href="/wiki/Coma_(U.S._miniseries)" title="Coma (U.S. miniseries)">miniseries</a> based on <a href="/wiki/Robin_Cook_(novelist)" class="mw-redirect" title="Robin Cook (novelist)">Robin Cook</a>\'s novel, <i><a href="/wiki/Coma_(novel)" title="Coma (novel)">Coma</a></i> for <a href="/wiki/A%26E_(TV_channel)" title="A&amp;E (TV channel)">A&amp;E</a>. The two-part miniseries premiered on A&amp;E on 3 September 2012, to mixed reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, Ridley stated that he is an <a href="/wiki/Atheist" class="mw-redirect" title="Atheist">atheist</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Ridley has dedicated several of his films in memory of his family: <i><a href="/wiki/Blade_Runner" title="Blade Runner">Blade Runner</a></i> to his brother Frank, <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Hawk_Down_(film)" title="Black Hawk Down (film)">Black Hawk Down</a></i> to his mother, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Counselor" title="The Counselor">The Counselor</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Exodus:_Gods_and_Kings" title="Exodus: Gods and Kings">Exodus: Gods and Kings</a></i> to his brother Tony.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Ridley also paid tribute to his late brother Tony at the 2016 Golden Globes, after his film, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Martian_(film)" title="The Martian (film)">The Martian</a></i>, won Best Motion Picture \xe2\x80\x93 Musical or Comedy.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When asked by the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> in a September 2014 interview if he believes in God, Scott replied:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>I\'m not sure. I think there\'s all kinds of questions raised... that\'s such an exotic question. If we looked at the whole thing practically speaking, the big bang occurred and then we go through this evolution of millions, billions of years where, by coincidence, all the right biological accidents came out the right way. To an extent, that doesn\'t make sense unless there was a controlling decider or mediator in all of that. So who was that? Or what was that? Are we one big grand experiment in the basic overall blink of the universe, or the galaxy? In which case, who is behind it? Maybe we\'re an experiment which can last a billion years, but which is a blink in their terms and they can then say: \'Right that didn\'t work, let\'s blow them up!\'<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Approach_and_style">Approach and style</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ridley_Scott&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Approach and style">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Appearing in the lead role in Scott\'s <i>Gladiator</i> and <i>Robin Hood</i>, <a href="/wiki/Russell_Crowe" title="Russell Crowe">Russell Crowe</a> commented, "I like being on Ridley\'s set because actors can perform [...] and the focus is on the performers."<sup id="cite_ref-gangster_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gangster-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Paul M. Sammon, in his book <i>Future Noir: The Making of Blade Runner</i>, commented in an interview with Brmovie.com that Scott\'s relationship with his actors has improved considerably over the years.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> More recently during the filming of Scott\'s 2012 film, <i><a href="/wiki/Prometheus_(2012_film)" title="Prometheus (2012 film)">Prometheus</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Charlize_Theron" title="Charlize Theron">Charlize Theron</a> praised the director\'s willingness to listen to suggestions from the cast for improvements in the way their characters are portrayed on screen. Theron worked alongside the writers and Scott to give more depth to her character during filming.<sup id="cite_ref-Prometheus_Theron_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Prometheus_Theron-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Scott\'s work is identified for its striking visuals, with <a href="/wiki/Girl_Power_in_popular_culture#Female_action_heroes_and_science_fiction" class="mw-redirect" title="Girl Power in popular culture">heroines</a> also a common theme.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Heroines_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heroines-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Female_heroes_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Female_heroes-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> His visual style, incorporating a detailed approach to production design and innovative, atmospheric lighting, has been influential on a subsequent generation of filmmakers.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Visual_style_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Visual_style-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Scott commonly uses slow pacing until the action sequences. Examples include <i>Alien</i> and <i>Blade Runner</i>; the <i>LA Times</i> critic Sheila Benson, for example, would call the latter "Blade Crawler" "because it\'s so damn slow". Another technique he employs is use of sound or music to build tension, as heard in <i>Alien</i>, with hissing steam, beeping computers and the noise of the machinery in the space ship. Scott claims to have an <a href="/wiki/Eidetic_memory" title="Eidetic memory">eidetic memory</a>, which he says aids him in visualising and storyboarding the scenes in his films.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Scott has developed a method for filming intricate shots as swiftly as possible: "I like working, always, with a minimum of three cameras. [...] So those 50 set-ups [a day] might only be 25 set-ups except I\'m covering in the set-up. So you\'re finished. I mean, if you take a little bit more time to prep on three cameras, or if it\'s a big stunt, eleven cameras, and&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 whilst it may take 45 minutes to set up&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 then when you\'re ready you say \'Action!\', and you do three takes, two takes and is everybody happy? You say, \'Yeah, that\'s it.\' So you move on."<sup id="cite_ref-gangster_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gangster-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">Artificial intelligence</a> is a unifying theme throughout Scott\'s career as a director, particularly in <i><a href="/wiki/Blade_Runner" title="Blade Runner">Blade Runner</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Alien_(film)" title="Alien (film)">Alien</a></i>, and <i>Prometheus</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> The recent book <i>The Culture and Philosophy of Ridley Scott</i> identifies <a href="/wiki/Alan_Turing" title="Alan Turing">Alan Turing</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Searle" title="John Searle">John Searle</a>, a professor at the University of California, as presenting relevant models of testing artificial intelligence known as the <a href="/wiki/Turing_test" title="Turing test">Turing test</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Room" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese Room">Chinese Room</a> Thought Experiment, respectively, in the chapter titled "What\'s Wrong with Building Replicants," which has been a recurring theme for many of Scott\'s films.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> The chapter titled "Artificial Intelligence in <i>Blade Runner</i>, <i>Alien</i>, and <i>Prometheus</i>," concludes by citing the writings of <a href="/wiki/John_Stuart_Mill" title="John Stuart Mill">John Stuart Mill</a> in the context of Scott\'s Nexus-6 Replicants in <i>Blade Runner</i> (Rutger Hauer), the android <a href="/wiki/Ash_(Alien)" title="Ash (Alien)">Ash</a> (Ian Holm) in <i>Alien</i>, and the android <a href="/wiki/David_8" title="David 8">David 8</a> (Michael Fassbender) in <i>Prometheus</i>, where Mill is applied to assert that measures and tests of intelligence must also assess actions and moral behaviour in androids to effectively address the themes which Scott explores in these films.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="DVD_format_and_Director.27s_Cut"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="DVD_format_and_Director\'s_Cut">DVD format and Director\'s Cut</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ridley_Scott&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: DVD format and Director&#039;s Cut">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Scott is known for his enthusiasm for the DVD format, providing <a href="/wiki/Audio_commentary_(DVD)" class="mw-redirect" title="Audio commentary (DVD)">audio commentaries</a> and interviews for all his films where possible. In the July 2006 issue of <i><a href="/wiki/Total_Film" title="Total Film">Total Film</a></i> magazine, he stated: "After all the work we go through, to have it run in the cinema and then disappear forever is a great pity. To give the film added life is really cool for both those who missed it and those who really loved it."<sup id="cite_ref-totalfilm_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-totalfilm-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Running alongside his enthusiasm for DVD, Scott is known for his use of the <a href="/wiki/Director%27s_cut" title="Director&#39;s cut">director\'s cut</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kingdom_63-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kingdom-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The positive reaction to the <i>Blade Runner</i> Director\'s Cut encouraged Scott to re-cut several movies that were a disappointment at the time of their release (including <i>Legend</i> and <i>Kingdom of Heaven</i>), which have been met with great acclaim.<sup id="cite_ref-Kingdom_63-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kingdom-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Today the practice of alternative cuts is more commonplace, though often as a way to make a film stand out in the DVD marketplace by adding new material.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Filmography_and_box_office_performance">Filmography and box office performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ridley_Scott&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Filmography and box office
